					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Open-source blockchain computing platform</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1257001546">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output (programming language)">Rust</a>, <a href="/wiki/C_Sharp_(programming_language)" title="C Sharp (programming language)">C#</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a>, <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a>, <a class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">Available in</a></th><td class="infobox-data">Multilingual, but primarily English</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/List_of_software_categories" class="mw-redirect" title="List of software categories">Type</a></th><td licenses</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap">Active hosts</th><td class="infobox-data">~8,600 nodes (6 June 2023)<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ethereum.org">ethereum<wbr />.org</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Ethereum</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Decentralization#Blockchain_technology" title="Decentralization">decentralized</a> <a href="/wiki/Blockchain" title="Blockchain">blockchain</a> with <a href="/wiki/Smart_contract" title="Smart contract">smart contract</a> functionality. <b>Ether</b> (<a href="/wiki/ISO_4217#Cryptocurrencies" title="ISO 4217">abbreviation</a>: <b>ETH</b><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>a<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>) is the native <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency" title="Cryptocurrency">cryptocurrency</a> of the platform. Among cryptocurrencies, ether is second only to <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin" title="Bitcoin">bitcoin</a> in <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ft20210528_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft20210528-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wsj20210603_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj20210603-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">open-source software</a>.
</p><p>Ethereum was conceived in 2013 by <a href="/wiki/Computer_programming" title="Computer programming">programmer</a> <a href="/wiki/Vitalik_Buterin" title="Vitalik Buterin">Vitalik Buterin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETapscottTapscott201687_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETapscottTapscott201687-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other founders include <a href="/wiki/Gavin_Wood" title="Gavin Wood">Gavin Wood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Hoskinson" title="Charles Hoskinson">Charles Hoskinson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Di_Iorio" title="Anthony Di Iorio">Anthony Di Iorio</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Lubin_(entrepreneur)" title="Joseph Lubin (entrepreneur)">Joseph Lubin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-paumgarten_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paumgarten-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2014, <a href="/wiki/Software_development" title="Software development">development</a> work began and was <a href="/wiki/Crowdfunding" title="Crowdfunding">crowdfunded</a>, and the network went live on 30 July 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ethereum allows anyone to deploy <a href="/wiki/Decentralized_application" title="Decentralized application">decentralized applications</a> onto it, with which users can interact.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Decentralized_finance" title="Decentralized finance">Decentralized finance</a> (DeFi) applications provide <a href="/wiki/Financial_instrument" title="Financial instrument">financial instruments</a> that do not directly rely on <a href="/wiki/Financial_intermediary" title="Financial intermediary">financial intermediaries</a> like <a href="/wiki/Brokerage" class="mw-redirect" title="Brokerage">brokerages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exchange_(organized_market)" title="Exchange (organized market)">exchanges</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Bank" title="Bank">banks</a>. This facilitates borrowing against cryptocurrency holdings or lending them out for <a href="/wiki/Interest" title="Interest">interest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fortune20210506_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortune20210506-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ethereum also allows users to create and exchange <a href="/wiki/Non-fungible_token" title="Non-fungible token">non-fungible tokens</a> (NFTs), which are tokens that can be tied to unique digital assets, such as images. Additionally, many other cryptocurrencies utilize the ERC-20 token standard on top of the Ethereum blockchain and have utilized the platform for <a href="/wiki/Initial_coin_offering" title="Initial coin offering">initial coin offerings</a>.
</p><p>On 15 September 2022, Ethereum transitioned its <a href="/wiki/Consensus_(computer_science)" title="Consensus (computer science)">consensus mechanism</a> from <a href="/wiki/Proof_of_work" title="Proof of work">proof-of-work</a> (PoW) to <a href="/wiki/Proof_of_stake" title="Proof of stake">proof-of-stake</a> (PoS) in an update known as "The Merge", which cut the blockchain's energy usage by 99%.<sup id="cite_ref-EnergyRevamp_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EnergyRevamp-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Founding_(2013–2014)"><span id="Founding_.282013.E2.80.932014.29"></span>Founding (2013–2014)</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Vitalik_Buterin_TechCrunch_London_2015_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Vitalik_Buterin_TechCrunch_London_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/262px-Vitalik_Buterin_TechCrunch_London_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="262" height="292" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Vitalik_Buterin_TechCrunch_London_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/393px-Vitalik_Buterin_TechCrunch_London_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Vitalik_Buterin_TechCrunch_London_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/524px-Vitalik_Buterin_TechCrunch_London_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3223" data-file-height="3597" /></a><figcaption>Ethereum co-founder <a href="/wiki/Vitalik_Buterin" title="Vitalik Buterin">Vitalik Buterin</a> in 2015</figcaption></figure>
<p>Ethereum was initially described in late 2013 in a <a href="/wiki/White_paper" title="White paper">white paper</a> by <a href="/wiki/Vitalik_Buterin" title="Vitalik Buterin">Vitalik Buterin</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETapscottTapscott201687_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETapscottTapscott201687-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> a programmer and co-founder of <i><a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_Magazine" title="Bitcoin Magazine">Bitcoin Magazine</a></i>, that described a way to build <a href="/wiki/Decentralized" class="mw-redirect" title="Decentralized">decentralized</a> applications.<sup id="cite_ref-Finley-27-Jan-2014_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Finley-27-Jan-2014-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Schneider-2014-04-07_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schneider-2014-04-07-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Buterin argued to the <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin_Core" title="Bitcoin Core">Bitcoin Core</a> developers that blockchain technology could benefit from other applications besides money and that it needed a more robust language for application development<sup id="cite_ref-tapscott2016_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tapscott2016-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 88">&#58;&#8202;88&#8202;</span></sup> that could lead to <span class="cleanup-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:var(--color-subtle, #54595d); border:1px solid var(--border-color-subtle, #c8ccd1);">attaching</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (March 2022)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> real-world assets, such as stocks and property, to the blockchain.<sup id="cite_ref-Russo2020_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Russo2020-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2013, Buterin briefly worked with <a href="/wiki/EToro" title="EToro">eToro</a> CEO Yoni Assia on the <a href="/wiki/Colored_Coins" title="Colored Coins">Colored Coins</a> project and drafted its white paper outlining additional use cases for blockchain technology.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERusso202044_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERusso202044-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, after failing to gain agreement on how the project should proceed, he proposed the development of a new platform with a more robust scripting language—a <a href="/wiki/Turing-complete" class="mw-redirect" title="Turing-complete">Turing-complete</a> programming language<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETapscottTapscott2016278_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETapscottTapscott2016278-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>—that would eventually become Ethereum.<sup id="cite_ref-tapscott2016_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tapscott2016-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Ethereum was announced at the North American Bitcoin Conference in Miami, in January 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Paumgarten_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paumgarten-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the conference, <a href="/wiki/Gavin_Wood" title="Gavin Wood">Gavin Wood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Hoskinson" title="Charles Hoskinson">Charles Hoskinson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Di_Iorio" title="Anthony Di Iorio">Anthony Di Iorio</a> (who financed the project) rented a house in Miami with Buterin at which they could develop a fuller sense of what Ethereum might become.<sup id="cite_ref-Paumgarten_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paumgarten-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Di Iorio invited friend <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Lubin_(entrepreneur)" title="Joseph Lubin (entrepreneur)">Joseph Lubin</a>, who invited reporter Morgen Peck, to bear witness.<sup id="cite_ref-Paumgarten_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paumgarten-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Peck subsequently wrote about the experience in <i><a href="/wiki/Wired_(magazine)" title="Wired (magazine)">Wired</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Six months later the founders met again in <a href="/wiki/Zug" title="Zug">Zug</a>, Switzerland, where Buterin told the founders that the project would proceed as a non-profit. Hoskinson left the project at that time and soon after founded IOHK, a blockchain company responsible for <a href="/wiki/Cardano_(blockchain_platform)" title="Cardano (blockchain platform)">Cardano</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Paumgarten_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paumgarten-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Ethereum has an unusually long list of founders.<sup id="cite_ref-entrepreneur20210817_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-entrepreneur20210817-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Anthony Di Iorio wrote: "Ethereum was founded by Vitalik Buterin, Myself, Charles Hoskinson, Mihai Alisie &amp; Amir Chetrit (the initial 5) in December 2013. Joseph Lubin, Gavin Wood, &amp; Jeffrey Wilcke were added in early 2014 as founders." Buterin chose the name Ethereum after browsing <a href="/wiki/List_of_fictional_elements,_materials,_isotopes_and_subatomic_particles" title="List of fictional elements, materials, isotopes and subatomic particles">a list of elements from science fiction</a> on <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a>. He stated, "I immediately realized that I liked it better than all of the other alternatives that I had seen; I suppose it was that [it] sounded nice and it had the word '<a href="/wiki/Luminiferous_aether" title="Luminiferous aether">ether</a>', referring to the hypothetical invisible medium that permeates the universe and allows light to travel."<sup id="cite_ref-Paumgarten_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paumgarten-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Buterin wanted his platform to be the underlying and imperceptible medium for the applications running on top of it.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERusso202056_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERusso202056-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Development_(2014)"><span id="Development_.282014.29"></span>Development (2014)</h3></div>
<p>Formal development of the software underlying Ethereum began in early 2014 through a Swiss company, Ethereum Switzerland GmbH (<i>EthSuisse</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg20160820_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg20160820-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
The idea of putting executable <a href="/wiki/Smart_contract" title="Smart contract">smart contracts</a> in the blockchain needed to be specified before it could be implemented in software. This work was done by Gavin Wood, then the <a href="/wiki/Chief_technology_officer" title="Chief technology officer">chief technology officer</a>, in the Ethereum Yellow Paper that specified the Ethereum Virtual Machine.<sup id="cite_ref-Dannen2018_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dannen2018-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eip150_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eip150-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Subsequently, a Swiss non-profit foundation, the <b>Ethereum Foundation</b> (<i>Stiftung Ethereum</i>), was founded. Development was funded by an online public crowd sale from July to August 2014, in which participants bought the Ethereum value token (ether) with another digital currency, <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin" title="Bitcoin">bitcoin</a>. While there was early praise for the technical innovations of Ethereum, questions were also raised about its security and scalability.<sup id="cite_ref-Finley-27-Jan-2014_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Finley-27-Jan-2014-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Foundation funded multiple teams in different cities building three separate implementations of the protocol: Geth (<a href="/wiki/Go_(programming_language)" title="Go (programming language)">Go</a>), Pyethereum (<a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a>), a <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a> implementation, and also Swarm (<a href="/wiki/Decentralized_file_storage" class="mw-redirect" title="Decentralized file storage">decentralized file storage</a>), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mist_Browser&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mist Browser (page does not exist)">Mist Browser</a> (A wallet, <a href="/wiki/File_browser" class="mw-redirect" title="File browser">browser</a> and a user interface for smart contracts, now defunct) among other projects. The intended purpose of the three distinct implementations would be so that if one of them had a bug, the other two could be used as a comparison.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Launch_and_the_DAO_event_(2014–2016)"><span id="Launch_and_the_DAO_event_.282014.E2.80.932016.29"></span>Launch and the DAO event (2014–2016)</h3></div>
<p>Several codenamed prototypes of Ethereum were developed over 18 months in 2014 and 2015 by the Ethereum Foundation as part of their <a href="/wiki/Proof_of_concept#Software_development" title="Proof of concept">proof-of-concept</a> series.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETapscottTapscott201687_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETapscottTapscott201687-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> "Olympic" was the last prototype and public beta pre-release. The Olympic network gave users a <a href="/wiki/Bug_bounty" class="mw-redirect" title="Bug bounty">bug bounty</a> of 25,000 ether for stress-testing the Ethereum blockchain. On 30 July 2015, "Frontier" marked the official launch of the Ethereum platform, and Ethereum created its "genesis block".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETapscottTapscott201687_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETapscottTapscott201687-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WSJFRONTIER_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJFRONTIER-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The genesis block contained 8,893 transactions allocating various amounts of ether to different addresses, and a block reward of 5 ETH.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Since the initial launch, Ethereum has undergone a number of planned protocol upgrades, which are important changes affecting the underlying functionality and/or <a href="/wiki/Incentive_compatibility" title="Incentive compatibility">incentive structures</a> of the platform.<sup id="cite_ref-EFPROCESS_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EFPROCESS-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Protocol upgrades are accomplished by means of a <a href="/wiki/Hard_fork" class="mw-redirect" title="Hard fork">hard fork</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 2016, a <a href="/wiki/Decentralized_autonomous_organization" title="Decentralized autonomous organization">decentralized autonomous organization</a> called <a href="/wiki/The_DAO_(organization)" class="mw-redirect" title="The DAO (organization)">The DAO</a>—a set of smart contracts developed on the platform—raised a record <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$150 million</span> in a <a href="/wiki/Token_sale" class="mw-redirect" title="Token sale">crowd sale</a> to fund the project.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJDAOCC_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJDAOCC-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Emin_G%C3%BCn_Sirer" title="Emin Gün Sirer">Emin Gün Sirer</a>, Vlad Zamfir and Dino Mark had written a paper called <i>A Call for a Temporary Moratorium on The DAO</i> in which they described in which way the DAO might be vunerable to attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-DAO_paper_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DAO_paper-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The DAO was exploited in June 2016 when <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$50 million</span> of DAO tokens were stolen by an unknown hacker.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTDAOHACK_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTDAOHACK-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BIDAOHACK_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BIDAOHACK-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The event sparked a debate in the crypto-community about whether Ethereum should perform a contentious "hard fork" to reappropriate the affected funds.<sup id="cite_ref-IEEEDAOHK_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEEEDAOHK-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The fork resulted in the network splitting into two blockchains: Ethereum with the theft reversed, and <a href="/wiki/Ethereum_Classic" title="Ethereum Classic">Ethereum Classic</a> which continued on the original chain.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg20170613_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg20170613-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Continued_development_and_milestones_(2017–present)"><span id="Continued_development_and_milestones_.282017.E2.80.93present.29"></span>Continued development and milestones (2017–present)</h3></div>
<p>In March 2017, various <a href="/wiki/Blockchain" title="Blockchain">blockchain</a> startups, research groups, and <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500"><i>Fortune</i> 500</a> companies announced the creation of the Enterprise Ethereum Alliance (EEA) with 30 founding members.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTEEA_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTEEA-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By May 2017, the nonprofit organization had 116 enterprise members, including <a href="/wiki/ConsenSys" class="mw-redirect" title="ConsenSys">ConsenSys</a>, <a href="/wiki/CME_Group" title="CME Group">CME Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University#Research" title="Cornell University">Cornell University's research group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Group" title="Toyota Group">Toyota Research Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samsung_SDS" title="Samsung SDS">Samsung SDS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a>, <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">J. P. Morgan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cooley_LLP" title="Cooley LLP">Cooley LLP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merck_KGaA" class="mw-redirect" title="Merck KGaA">Merck KGaA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Depository_Trust_%26_Clearing_Corporation" title="Depository Trust &amp; Clearing Corporation">DTCC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deloitte" title="Deloitte">Deloitte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accenture" title="Accenture">Accenture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banco_Santander" title="Banco Santander">Banco Santander</a>, <a href="/wiki/BNY_Mellon" class="mw-redirect" title="BNY Mellon">BNY Mellon</a>, <a href="/wiki/ING_Group" title="ING Group">ING</a>, and <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Canada" title="National Bank of Canada">National Bank of Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IEEEEEA_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEEEEEA-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EEA022217_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EEA022217-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By July 2017, there were over 150 members in the alliance, including <a href="/wiki/MasterCard" class="mw-redirect" title="MasterCard">MasterCard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cisco_Systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Cisco Systems">Cisco Systems</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sberbank" title="Sberbank">Sberbank</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scotiabank" title="Scotiabank">Scotiabank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2024, Paul Brody, EEA board member for EY, was announced as the new chairperson, and Karen Scarbrough, board member for Microsoft, as the new executive director. Vanessa Grellet from Arche Capital also joined as a new board member.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="CryptoKitties_and_the_ERC-721_NFT_standard"><i>CryptoKitties</i> and the ERC-721 NFT standard</h4></div>
<p>In 2017, <i><a href="/wiki/CryptoKitties" title="CryptoKitties">CryptoKitties</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Blockchain_game" title="Blockchain game">blockchain game</a> and <a href="/wiki/Decentralized_application" title="Decentralized application">decentralized application</a> (dApp) featuring digital cat artwork as <a href="/wiki/Non-fungible_token" title="Non-fungible token">NFTs</a>, was launched on the Ethereum network.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In cultivating popularity with users and collectors, it gained notable mainstream media attention providing significant exposure to Ethereum in the process.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was considered the most popular smart contract in use on the network<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but it also highlighted concerns over Ethereum's scalability due to the game's substantial consumption of network capacity at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2018, a community-driven paper (an EIP, "Ethereum Improvement Proposal") under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Hacker#Civic_hacker" title="Hacker">civic hacker</a> and lead author <a href="/wiki/William_Entriken" title="William Entriken">William Entriken</a> was published, called <i>ERC-721: Non-Fungible Token Standard.</i><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It introduced <a href="/wiki/ERC-721" title="ERC-721">ERC-721</a>, the first official NFT standard on Ethereum.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This standardization allowed Ethereum to become central to a multi-billion dollar digital collectibles market.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Continued_developments">Continued developments</h4></div>
<p>By January 2018, ether was the second-largest cryptocurrency in terms of market capitalization, behind bitcoin.<sup id="cite_ref-fortune20180108_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortune20180108-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of 2021<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ethereum&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, it maintained that relative position.<sup id="cite_ref-ft20210528_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft20210528-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wsj20210603_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj20210603-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019, Ethereum Foundation employee <a href="/wiki/Virgil_Griffith" title="Virgil Griffith">Virgil Griffith</a> was arrested by the US government for presenting at a blockchain conference in North Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He would later plead guilty to one count of conspiring to violate the International Emergency Economic Powers Act in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2021, <a href="/wiki/Visa_Inc." title="Visa Inc.">Visa Inc.</a> announced that it began settling <a href="/wiki/Stablecoin" title="Stablecoin">stablecoin</a> transactions using Ethereum.<sup id="cite_ref-fortune20210329_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortune20210329-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In April 2021, <a href="/wiki/JP_Morgan_Chase" class="mw-redirect" title="JP Morgan Chase">JP Morgan Chase</a>, <a href="/wiki/UBS" title="UBS">UBS</a>, and <a href="/wiki/MasterCard" class="mw-redirect" title="MasterCard">MasterCard</a> announced that they were investing <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$65 million</span> into <a href="/wiki/ConsenSys" class="mw-redirect" title="ConsenSys">ConsenSys</a>, a software development firm that builds Ethereum-related infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-fortune20210413_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortune20210413-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>There were two network upgrades in 2021. The first was "Berlin", implemented on 14 April 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-bi20210413_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bi20210413-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The second was "London", which took effect on 5 August.<sup id="cite_ref-cnbc20210805_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnbc20210805-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The London upgrade included Ethereum Improvement Proposal ("EIP") 1559, a mechanism for reducing transaction fee <a href="/wiki/Volatility_(finance)" title="Volatility (finance)">volatility</a>. The mechanism causes a portion of the ether paid in transaction fees for each block to be destroyed rather than given to the block proposer, reducing the inflation rate of ether and potentially resulting in periods of deflation.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg20210307_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg20210307-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 27 August 2021, the blockchain experienced a brief <a href="/wiki/Fork_(blockchain)" title="Fork (blockchain)">fork</a> that was the result of clients running different incompatible software versions.<sup id="cite_ref-bloom20210827_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloom20210827-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="The_Merge:_Transition_from_Proof-of-Work_to_Proof-of-Stake">The Merge: Transition from Proof-of-Work to Proof-of-Stake</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ethereum_Merge_Party_in_San_Francisco_in_2022.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Ethereum_Merge_Party_in_San_Francisco_in_2022.jpg/220px-Ethereum_Merge_Party_in_San_Francisco_in_2022.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="243" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Ethereum_Merge_Party_in_San_Francisco_in_2022.jpg/330px-Ethereum_Merge_Party_in_San_Francisco_in_2022.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Ethereum_Merge_Party_in_San_Francisco_in_2022.jpg/440px-Ethereum_Merge_Party_in_San_Francisco_in_2022.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2268" data-file-height="2509" /></a><figcaption>Ethereum enthusiasts gather for a Merge party in San Francisco in 2022.</figcaption></figure>
<p>"The Merge" (formerly called Ethereum 2.0) was a set of three updated (Bellatrix, Paris, and Shapella) that transitioned Ethereum's consensus protocol from Proof-of-Work to Proof-of-Stake. Bellatrix updated the Proof-of-Stake Beacon chain and introduced economic slashing. Paris was the event at block 15537393 on 15th September 2022 that merged Ethereum to the Beacon chain. Shapella (Shanghai-Capella) was the update that allowed for staking withdrawals.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The switch from proof-of-work to proof-of-stake on 15 September 2022 has cut Ethereum's energy usage by over 99%.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, the impact this has on <a href="/wiki/Global_energy_consumption" class="mw-redirect" title="Global energy consumption">global energy consumption</a> and climate change may be limited since the computers previously used for mining ether may be used to mine other cryptocurrencies that are energy-intensive.<sup id="cite_ref-EnergyRevamp_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EnergyRevamp-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Post-Merge_updates">Post-Merge updates</h3></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Dencun">Dencun</h4></div>
<p>On March 13, 2024, "Dencun" or also "Deneb-Cancun" set of upgrade went live. These included EIP-4844 (Proto-Danksharding) which introduced "blobs" that could be used for general-purpose data-availability. Because "Blob" data is only stored temporarily, it is much cheaper than using normal call data for storage. This allows for L2 networks to greatly reduce the cost of posting compressed transaction data to L1.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Pectra">Pectra</h4></div>
<p>According to Ethereum.org, Prague-Electra ("Pectra") is expected to be launched in mid-2025. It brings various updates, including EIP-7251, which increases the staking amount per validator from exactly 32 ETH to anywhere between 32 ETH to 2048 ETH, and EIP-7702, which allows for the EOA addresses to use functionality from a smart contract.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Design">Design</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Overview">Overview</h3></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1251242444">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .ambox{display:none!important}}</style><table class="box-Primary_sources plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Primary_sources" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>relies excessively on <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">references</a> to <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research">primary sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please improve this section by adding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research">secondary or tertiary sources</a>.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2024</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Ethereum is a <a href="/wiki/Peer-to-peer_network" class="mw-redirect" title="Peer-to-peer network">peer-to-peer network</a> that maintains a <a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">database</a> containing the storage values of all Ethereum accounts and processes state-altering transactions.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Approximately every 12 seconds, a batch of new transactions, known as a "block", is processed by the network. Each block contains a <a href="/wiki/Cryptographic_hash_function" title="Cryptographic hash function">cryptographic hash</a> identifying the series of blocks that must precede it if the block is to be considered valid. This series of blocks is known as the <a href="/wiki/Blockchain" title="Blockchain">blockchain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Each "node" (network participant) connects with a relatively small subset of the network to offer blocks and unvalidated transactions (i.e. transactions not yet in the blockchain) to its peers for download, and it downloads any of these from its peers that it doesn't already have. Each node usually has a unique set of peers, so that offering an item to its peers results in the propagation of that item throughout the entire network within seconds. A node's collection of unvalidated transactions is known as its "mempool".<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A node may choose to create a copy of the state for itself. It does this by starting with the genesis state and executing every transaction in the blockchain, in the proper order of blocks and in the order they are listed within each block.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Any Ethereum account may "stake" (deposit) 32 ETH to become a validator. At the end of each "epoch" (32 block slots, each slot lasting 12 seconds), each validator is <a href="/wiki/Pseudorandomness" title="Pseudorandomness">pseudorandomly</a> assigned to one of the slots of the epoch after the next, either as the block proposer or as an attester. During a slot, the block proposer uses their mempool to create a block that is intended to become the new "head" (latest block) of the blockchain, and the attesters attest to which block is at the head of the chain. If a validator makes self-contradicting proposals or attestations, or if it is inactive, it loses a portion of its stake. It may add to its stake at any time. A validator's attestation is given a weight equal to its stake or 32, whichever is less. According to the Ethereum protocol, the blockchain with the highest accumulated weight of attestations at any given time is to be regarded as the canonical chain. Validators are rewarded for making valid proposals and attestations. A validator's rewards are paid via transactions within the same chain that contains their proposal or attestation, and therefore would have little or no market value unless that chain becomes the canonical chain. This incentivizes validators to support the chain that they think other validators view as the canonical chain, which results in a high degree of consensus.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Ether">Ether</h3></div>
<p>Ether (ETH) is the cryptocurrency generated in accordance with the Ethereum protocol as a reward to validators in a <a href="/wiki/Proof_of_stake" title="Proof of stake">proof-of-stake</a> system for adding blocks to the blockchain. Ether is represented in the state as an <a href="/wiki/Signedness" title="Signedness">unsigned</a> <a href="/wiki/Integer_(computer_science)" title="Integer (computer science)">integer</a> associated with each account, this being the account's ETH balance denominated in wei (10<sup>18</sup> wei = 1 ether). At the end of each epoch, new ETH is generated by the addition of protocol-specified amounts to the balances of all validators that made valid block proposals or attestations in the epoch before the last (i.e. the epoch being finalized). Additionally, ether is the only currency accepted by the protocol as payment for the transaction fee. The transaction fee is composed of two parts: the base fee and the tip. The base fee is "burned" (deleted from existence) and the tip goes to the block proposer. The validator reward together with the tips provide the incentive to validators to keep the blockchain growing (i.e. to keep processing new transactions). Therefore, ETH is fundamental to the operation of the network. Ether may be "sent" from one account to another via a transaction, the execution of which simply entails subtracting the <i>amount to be sent</i> from the sender's balance and adding the same amount to the recipient's balance.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTEVCRB_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTEVCRB-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Ether is often erroneously referred to as "Ethereum".<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The uppercase Greek letter <a href="/wiki/Xi_(letter)" title="Xi (letter)">Xi</a>, Ξ, is sometimes used as a <a href="/wiki/Currency_symbol" title="Currency symbol">currency symbol</a> for ether.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Accounts">Accounts</h3></div>
<p>There are two types of accounts on Ethereum: user accounts (also known as externally-owned accounts), and contract accounts. Both types have an ETH balance, may transfer ETH to any account, may execute the code of another contract, or create a new contract, and are identified on the blockchain and in the state by an account address.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg20201125_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg20201125-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Contracts are the only type of account that has associated <a href="/wiki/Bytecode" title="Bytecode">bytecode</a> and storage (to store contract-specific state). The code of a contract is evaluated when a transaction is sent to it. The code of the contract may read user-specified data from the transaction, and may have a <a href="/wiki/Return_statement" title="Return statement">return value</a>. In addition to <a href="/wiki/Control_flow" title="Control flow">control flow</a> statements, the bytecode may include instructions to send ETH, read from and write to the contract's storage, create temporary storage (<a href="/wiki/Volatile_memory" title="Volatile memory">memory</a>) that vanishes at the end of code evaluation, perform <a href="/wiki/Arithmetic" title="Arithmetic">arithmetic</a> and hashing operations, send transaction-like calls to other contracts (thus executing their code), create new contracts, and query information about the current transaction or the blockchain.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (May 2024)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Addresses">Addresses</h4></div>
<p>Ethereum addresses are composed of the prefix "<code>0x</code>" (a common identifier for <a href="/wiki/Hexadecimal" title="Hexadecimal">hexadecimal</a>) concatenated with the rightmost 20 bytes of the <a href="/wiki/SHA-3" title="SHA-3">Keccak-256</a> hash of the <a href="/wiki/Elliptic_Curve_Digital_Signature_Algorithm" title="Elliptic Curve Digital Signature Algorithm">ECDSA</a> <a href="/wiki/Public-key_cryptography" title="Public-key cryptography">public key</a> (the curve used is the so-called <i>secp256k1</i>). In hexadecimal, two digits represent a byte, and so addresses contain 40 hexadecimal digits after the "<code>0x</code>", e.g. <code>0xb794f5ea0ba39494ce839613fffba74279579268</code>. Contract addresses are in the same format, however, they are determined by sender and creation transaction <a href="/wiki/Cryptographic_nonce" title="Cryptographic nonce">nonce</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eip150_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eip150-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (May 2024)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Virtual_machine">Virtual machine</h3></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ethereum_Transactions_Chart.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Ethereum_Transactions_Chart.png/350px-Ethereum_Transactions_Chart.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="234" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Ethereum_Transactions_Chart.png/525px-Ethereum_Transactions_Chart.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Ethereum_Transactions_Chart.png/700px-Ethereum_Transactions_Chart.png 2x" data-file-width="1402" data-file-height="936" /></a><figcaption>The number of daily confirmed Ethereum transactions as of February 2024</figcaption></figure>
<p>The Ethereum Virtual Machine (EVM) is the <a href="/wiki/Runtime_(program_lifecycle_phase)" class="mw-redirect" title="Runtime (program lifecycle phase)">runtime</a> environment for transaction execution in Ethereum. The EVM is a <a href="/wiki/Stack_(abstract_data_type)" title="Stack (abstract data type)">stack</a> based virtual machine with an <a href="/wiki/Instruction_set_architecture" title="Instruction set architecture">instruction set</a> specifically designed for Ethereum. The instruction set includes, among other things, stack operations, memory operations, and operations to inspect the current execution context, such as remaining gas, information about the current block, and the current transaction. The EVM is designed to be <a href="/wiki/Deterministic_algorithm" title="Deterministic algorithm">deterministic</a> on a wide variety of <a href="/wiki/Computer_hardware" title="Computer hardware">hardware</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating systems</a>, so that given a pre-transaction state and a transaction, each node produces the same post-transaction state, thereby enabling network consensus. The formal definition of the EVM is specified in the Ethereum Yellow Paper.<sup id="cite_ref-eip150_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eip150-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DEBA20_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DEBA20-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> EVMs have been implemented in <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a>, <a href="/wiki/C_Sharp_(programming_language)" title="C Sharp (programming language)">C#</a>, <a href="/wiki/Go_(programming_language)" title="Go (programming language)">Go</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haskell_(programming_language)" class="mw-redirect" title="Haskell (programming language)">Haskell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a>, <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruby_(programming_language)" title="Ruby (programming language)">Ruby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rust_(programming_language)" title="Rust (programming language)">Rust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elixir_(programming_language)" title="Elixir (programming language)">Elixir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erlang_(programming_language)" title="Erlang (programming language)">Erlang</a>, and soon<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="This article has been claiming at least since 2018 that EVMs implemented in WebAssembly will come &quot;soon&quot;. (October 2021)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/WebAssembly" title="WebAssembly">WebAssembly</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Gas">Gas</h3></div>
<p>Gas is a <a href="/wiki/Unit_of_account" title="Unit of account">unit of account</a> within the EVM used in the calculation of the transaction fee, which is the amount of ETH a transaction's sender must pay to the network to have the transaction included in the blockchain. Each type of operation which may be performed by the EVM is <a href="/wiki/Hardcoded" class="mw-redirect" title="Hardcoded">hardcoded</a> with a certain gas cost, which is intended to be roughly <a href="/wiki/Proportionality_(mathematics)" title="Proportionality (mathematics)">proportional</a> to the monetary value of the resources (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Computation" title="Computation">computation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Computer_data_storage" title="Computer data storage">storage</a>) a node must expend or dedicate to perform that operation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>When a sender is creating a transaction, the sender must specify a <i>gas limit</i> and <i>gas price</i>. The <i>gas limit</i> is the maximum amount of gas the sender is willing to use in the transaction, and the <i>gas price</i> is the amount of ETH the sender wishes to pay to the network per unit of gas used. A transaction may only be included in the blockchain at a block slot that has a <i>base gas price</i> less than or equal to the transaction's <i>gas price</i>. The portion of the <i>gas price</i> that is in excess of the <i>base gas price</i> is known as the tip and goes to the block proposer; the higher the tip, the more incentive a block proposer has to include the transaction in their block, and thus the quicker the transaction will be included in the blockchain. The sender buys the full amount of gas (i.e. their ETH balance is debited <i>gas limit</i> × <i>gas price</i> and their gas balance is set to <i>gas limit</i>) up-front, at the start of the execution of the transaction, and is refunded at the end for any unused gas. If at any point the transaction does not have enough gas to perform the next operation, the transaction is reverted but the sender is still only refunded for the unused gas. In <a href="/wiki/User_interface" title="User interface">user interfaces</a>, gas prices are typically denominated in gigawei (Gwei), a subunit of ETH equal to 10<sup>−9</sup> ETH.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Applications">Applications<span class="anchor" id="ERC721"></span></h2></div>
<p>The EVM's <a href="/wiki/Instruction_set" class="mw-redirect" title="Instruction set">instruction set</a> is <a href="/wiki/Turing_completeness" title="Turing completeness">Turing-complete</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eip150_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eip150-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Popular uses of Ethereum have included the creation of fungible (ERC-20) and non-fungible (ERC-721) tokens with a variety of properties, <a href="/wiki/Crowdfunding" title="Crowdfunding">crowdfunding</a> (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Initial_coin_offerings" class="mw-redirect" title="Initial coin offerings">initial coin offerings</a>), <a href="/wiki/Decentralized_finance" title="Decentralized finance">decentralized finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Decentralized_exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Decentralized exchange">decentralized exchanges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Decentralized_autonomous_organization" title="Decentralized autonomous organization">decentralized autonomous organizations</a> (DAOs), games, <a href="/wiki/Prediction_market" title="Prediction market">prediction markets</a>, and gambling.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Contract_source_code">Contract source code</h3></div>
<p>Ethereum's smart contracts are written in <a href="/wiki/High-level_programming_language" title="High-level programming language">high-level</a> programming languages and then <a href="/wiki/Compiler" title="Compiler">compiled</a> down to EVM <a href="/wiki/Bytecode" title="Bytecode">bytecode</a>, which is then deployed to the Ethereum blockchain. They can be written in <a href="/wiki/Solidity" title="Solidity">Solidity</a> (a language library with similarities to <a href="/wiki/C_(programming_language)" title="C (programming language)">C</a> and <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a>), as well as others.  Source code and compiler information are usually published on blockchain explorer websites soon after the launch of the contract so that users can see the code and verify that it compiles to the bytecode that is on-chain.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>One issue related to using smart contracts on a public blockchain is that bugs, including security holes, are visible to all but cannot be fixed quickly.<sup id="cite_ref-Peck20160528_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peck20160528-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> One example of this is the 2016 attack on <a href="/wiki/The_DAO_(organization)" class="mw-redirect" title="The DAO (organization)">The DAO</a>, which could not be quickly stopped or reversed.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTDAOHACK_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTDAOHACK-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="ERC-20_tokens">ERC-20 tokens<span class="anchor" id="ERC20"></span></h3></div>
<p>The ERC-20 (Ethereum Request-for-Comments #20) Token Standard allows for <a href="/wiki/Fungible" class="mw-redirect" title="Fungible">fungible</a> tokens on the Ethereum <a href="/wiki/Blockchain" title="Blockchain">blockchain</a>. The standard, proposed by Fabian Vogelsteller in November 2015, implements an <a href="/wiki/API" title="API">API</a> for tokens within <a href="/wiki/Smart_contract" title="Smart contract">smart contracts</a>. The standard provides functions that include the transfer of tokens from one account to another, getting the current token balance of an account, and getting the total supply of the token available on the network. Smart contracts that correctly implement ERC-20 processes are called ERC-20 Token Contracts, and they keep track of created tokens on Ethereum. Numerous cryptocurrencies have launched as ERC-20 tokens and have been distributed through <a href="/wiki/Initial_coin_offerings" class="mw-redirect" title="Initial coin offerings">initial coin offerings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes20200728_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes20200728-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Non-fungible_tokens_(NFTs)"><span id="Non-fungible_tokens_.28NFTs.29"></span>Non-fungible tokens (NFTs)</h3></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Non-fungible_token" title="Non-fungible token">Non-fungible token</a></div>
<p>Ethereum also allows for the creation of unique and indivisible tokens, called <a href="/wiki/Non-fungible_token" title="Non-fungible token">non-fungible tokens</a> (NFTs).<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Since tokens of this type are unique, they have been used to represent such things as collectibles, digital art, sports memorabilia, virtual real estate, and items within games.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> ERC-721 is the first official NFT standard for Ethereum and was followed up by ERC-1155 which introduced semi-fungibility, both are widely used,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> though some fully fungible tokens using ERC-20 have been used for NFTs such as <i><a href="/wiki/CryptoPunks" title="CryptoPunks">CryptoPunks</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The first NFT project, Etheria, a 3D map of tradable and customizable hexagonal tiles, was deployed to the network in October 2015 and demonstrated live at DEVCON1 in November of that year.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2021, <a href="/wiki/Christie%27s" title="Christie&#39;s">Christie's</a> sold a digital image with an NFT by <a href="/wiki/Beeple" class="mw-redirect" title="Beeple">Beeple</a> for <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$69.3 million</span>, making him the <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_artworks_by_living_artists" title="List of most expensive artworks by living artists">third-most-valuable living artist</a> in terms of <a href="/wiki/Art_auction" title="Art auction">auction</a> prices at the time, although observers have noted that both the buyer and seller had a vested interest in driving demand for the artist's work.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Decentralized_finance">Decentralized finance</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Decentralized_finance" title="Decentralized finance">Decentralized finance</a></div>
<p>Decentralized finance (DeFi) offers <a href="/wiki/Financial_instrument" title="Financial instrument">financial instruments</a> in a decentralized architecture, outside of companies' and governments' control, such as money market funds which let users earn interest.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes20190426_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes20190426-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> DeFi applications are typically accessed through a <a href="/wiki/Web3" title="Web3">Web3</a>-enabled browser extension or application, such as <a href="/wiki/MetaMask" title="MetaMask">MetaMask</a>, which allows users to directly interact with the Ethereum blockchain through a website.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg20200902_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg20200902-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many of these DApps can connect and work together to create complex financial services.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg20200826_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg20200826-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Examples of DeFi platforms include <a href="/w/index.php?title=MakerDAO&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="MakerDAO (page does not exist)">MakerDAO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fortune20200825_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortune20200825-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Uniswap" title="Uniswap">Uniswap</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Decentralized_exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Decentralized exchange">decentralized exchange</a> for tokens on Ethereum grew from <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$20 million</span> in liquidity to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$2.9 billion</span> in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes20201018_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes20201018-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of October 2020, over <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$11 billion</span> was invested in various DeFi protocols.<sup id="cite_ref-Zcash_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zcash-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Additionally, through a process called "wrapping", certain DeFi protocols allow synthetic versions of various assets (such as bitcoin, gold, and oil) to be tradeable on Ethereum and also compatible with all of Ethereum's major wallets and applications.<sup id="cite_ref-Zcash_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zcash-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Enterprise_software">Enterprise software</h3></div>
<p>Ethereum-based software and networks, independent from the public Ethereum chain, have been tested by <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_software" title="Enterprise software">enterprise software</a> companies.<sup id="cite_ref-renamed_from_20170228_on_20210805181819_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-renamed_from_20170228_on_20210805181819-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Interested parties have included <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">JPMorgan Chase</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-NYTEVCRB_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTEVCRB-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Deloitte" title="Deloitte">Deloitte</a>, R3, and <a href="/wiki/Innovate_UK" title="Innovate UK">Innovate UK</a> (cross-border payments prototype).<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Barclays" title="Barclays">Barclays</a>, <a href="/wiki/UBS" title="UBS">UBS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Credit_Suisse" title="Credit Suisse">Credit Suisse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_(company)" title="Amazon (company)">Amazon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visa_Inc." title="Visa Inc.">Visa</a>, and other companies have also experimented with Ethereum.<sup id="cite_ref-renamed_from_20200219_on_20210805181819_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-renamed_from_20200219_on_20210805181819-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg20201203_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg20201203-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Permissioned_ledgers">Permissioned ledgers</h3></div>
<p>Ethereum-based <a href="/wiki/Blockchain_(database)#Openness" class="mw-redirect" title="Blockchain (database)">permissioned blockchain</a> variants are used and being investigated for various projects:
</p>
<ul><li>In 2017, <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">JPMorgan Chase</a> proposed developing <a href="/wiki/JPM_Coin" title="JPM Coin">JPM Coin</a> on a permissioned-variant of Ethereum blockchain dubbed "Quorum".<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is "designed to toe the line between private and public in the realm of shuffling derivatives and payments. The idea is to satisfy regulators who need seamless access to financial goings-on while protecting the privacy of parties that don't wish to reveal their identities nor the details of their transactions to the general public."<sup id="cite_ref-fortune20161014_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortune20161014-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Performance">Performance</h3></div>
<p>As of January 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ethereum&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the Ethereum protocol could process about 25 transactions per second; this did not change after the move to proof-of-stake. In comparison, the <a href="/wiki/Visa_Inc." title="Visa Inc.">Visa</a> payment platform processes 45,000 payments per second. This has led some to question the scalability of Ethereum.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A proposal to partition global state and computation into <a href="/wiki/Shard_(database_architecture)" title="Shard (database architecture)">shard chains</a> was presented at Ethereum's Devcon 3 in November 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> If implemented, each node in the network would only have to store and validate a subset of the network.
</p><p>Ethereum's blockchain uses a <a href="/wiki/Merkle_tree" title="Merkle tree">Merkle</a>–Patricia Tree to store account state in each block.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The trie allows for storage savings, set membership proofs (called "Merkle proofs"), and light client synchronization. The network has faced congestion problems, such as in 2017 in relation to <i><a href="/wiki/CryptoKitties" title="CryptoKitties">CryptoKitties</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Regulation">Regulation</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/2020s_commodities_boom" title="2020s commodities boom">2020s commodities boom</a></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, the proposed <a href="/wiki/Digital_Commodities_Consumer_Protection_Act" title="Digital Commodities Consumer Protection Act">Digital Commodities Consumer Protection Act</a> would treat Ethereum and other cryptocurrencies as <a href="/wiki/Commodity" title="Commodity">commodities</a>, which could then be regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Commodity_Futures_Trading_Commission" title="Commodity Futures Trading Commission">Commodity Futures Trading Commission</a> (CFTC).<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
